< Review>
Massage services and the massage therapists are quite nice. But ambiance gets 0 stars. It's impossible to fully disconnect when the treatment room is on street level on Laguna, where there's a constant flow of vehicle and foot traffic. The music over the speakers went out twice in our room before my massage therapist just went and got her phone as a stand in. Despite the music, you can still hear traffic outside, neighbors who live upstairs entering the building, and the din of staff chatting in the lobby area. The business is a tiny space, with the paper thin walls of classic SF homes. They do their best for a small business, but at their prices for a sub-optimal experience ($650 for a 2hr couple's treatment), we'll opt for a proper big name spa next time with more amenities and a guaranteed relaxing environment.</Review>

<text>Earthbody is my favorite place to go when I want to be completely nurtured.

First thing I notice when I get there is the ambiance. The decor is warm and pretty and a nice mixture of Moroccan inspired against the backdrop of San Francisco Victorian. The waiting room is a cozy space where you can relax, enjoy some books, drink some water, it's a really nice place to be.

Second, there is the exceptional professionalism of the staff. Someone will warmly greet you. The massage therapist will have a nice conversation with you about what you're hoping to get out of the massage, any pains, you have, etc. It's the conversation that pretty much all massage therapists have or should have before a treatment, but my experience with Earthbody therapists has always been top notch. The warmth, nurturing, and professionalism in their communications really shines through.

Third, the quality of the treatments. I've been here at least a half a dozen times. All of the massages I've experienced have been top quality. Great technique and very relaxing experience.

Last, there is usually a nice little send-off for you at the end. They might give you a little card on what do after your massage and a glass of water to drink and sometimes a little bite of chocolate or nuts/dried fruit to eat and you're back sitting in the lovely little waiting room and able to just regroup before you head back out to busy San Francisco.

Overall I highly recommend Earthbody.<//text>< Pictures>

< Review>
A massage at Earthbody is not just a massage, it's an incredible experience from start to finish.  As I arrive I feel the sanctuary around me and expanding from within. < text>
Hello fellow foodies, not real enthused with this place, yet keeping it real once again....

Came in for breakfast with the fam this morning after reading their reviews on Google and Yelp.

Initially observed they could have turned up their airconditioner a bit, it would be more comfortable in there. Considering it was a hot and exceptionally humid morning that extra cooling would have been appreciated.

In all fairness, the food was okay with particular emphasis and kudos on the thinly fried fish referred to as "jeprox". Real satisfying with garlic rice.

The "longanisa" was well seasoned and cooked quite well. Goes down real easy too.

A little dissapointed with the preparation of their "tocino", fried chicken, and adobo as they appeared undercooked and cold. Just couldn't handle more than two or three bites.  (...however in the spirit of fairness, the food looked appetizing in the  warmer.)

I really believe once they get their act together, this place definitely  has tremendous potential.

I will give Bamboo Bistro another try in a few months, and trust that appropriate changes will be made to secure and lock in my business.

See you guys then, I know you can do it guys! See you in a few months.

Thank you!< /text>

<text>Budol "fight" style.  Dont let that intimate you. First off, all "dry" food are laid out neatly in the middle of a table covered with banana leaves. The "fight" comes when you sit down and start serving yourself the most delicious Filipino comfort food. There's a convenient sink to wash your hands first.

< Review>
I've been here before for events with the family. It's kind of our go-to place when we dont want to cook Filipino food and worry about clean up afterwards. It's in a interesting location surrounded by Mexican restaurants and stores but it's been going strong within the community for a while and I hope it stays that way.

What's great about Bamboo Bistro is their sense of camaraderie and heritage for Filipino culture. They have karaoke nights, show Filipino television shows and they have "Kamayan" which is the traditional way of eating Filipino food; with your hands.

You don't have to speak tagalog to eat here either, you usually can just point at what looks good and it'll come with a side of rice. Just be weary if you're on a diet since Filipino food is like the Soul Food of Asia.

They also do catering orders *cash only*<//Review>

<Review>Hands down the best Filipino food in the area!!! You can experience the traditional filipino boodle fight, also known as "kamayan" which is a meal where banana leaves are laid out on the table and the food place down the center, and shared among the party, making it a real communal experience. They also have breakfast and lunch buffets on the weekends which provide an exceptional value for all you can eat Filipino food (I believe $9 for breakfast and $12 for lunch, I know they just increased the price on this recently).  My favorite dishes here are the Adobo Fried Rice and Pork Liempo, but every dish I've had here has been pretty damn delicious!</Review><pictures>None< /pictures>< Response>

<text>Although I have known about this restaurant for more than a year, this was our first time eating at this restaurant. We decided to eat Kamayan style which is the Filipino tradition of eating with your hands.

With Kamayan style, they basically lay banana leaves on the table and they put your food on top of the banana leaves. You use your hands to eat your food. Of course, you cant eat soup with your hands so they do provide you a bowl and a spoon for the soup. We ordered Kare-Kare, Crispy Pata, Talipia, Squid and a couple of other dishes. They were all good!
However, it does take a while to cook the dishes so if you are planning to eat Kamayan style, I would suggest you order before you come in or plan to wait 20-25 minutes for your food to be ready.

The location of the restaurant is in an odd place. It is in a shopping center surrounded by mostly Mexican businesses. It is the only Filipino business in the shopping center.< /text><pics>None</pics>< Response>

<Name>Tanner Bell</Name><Time>1490772074456< /Time><rate>1<//rate>< review>
If you're looking for a decent place to buy a drink, to get some food, or just socialize with friends, DONT GO HERE!!! The food portions were incredibly small, the word from multiple employees here is incredibly unaccountable, and the environment is very disrespectful. From someone who is pretty low-key and relaxed at bars, I had a terrible experience here, along with several other people at the random night I went:

- No kidding, the bar tenders were looking to pick fights with some people asking questions about the promotion.
- It was taco night and they ran out of tacos (which was the sole reason I came)
- The owner said the f-word to several customers and wore a shirt that said "F*** B*****s and get drunk. Be like me". Which was a pretty good reflection of the kind of culture this bar had.
- Multiple employees were smoking at the entrance to the bar, which was unpleasant to people that don't smoke cigarettes
- It wasn't easy to park here and it I did not feel safe while I was in the parking lot (which this is the fist bar I can ever say that about).

If you are looking for some good bars here are some around the area I would suggest!
- The Congregation
- Rude Dogs (no ones actually rude here).</review>
